## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population P. This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through various density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, often used in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with critical minimum population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling in growth)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Power-law growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric scaling of growth rate with population size)
- Density-dependent with time variation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t) (logistic growth with time-varying parameters)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic density-dependent growth)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting/immigration)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → Quadratic terms in P such as P*(1 - P/K) or equivalently c0*P + c1*P**2
- Allee effects (positive density dependence at low P) → Cubic or higher-order polynomial in P with sign changes, e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P)
- Metabolic scaling in growth → Fractional power-law terms like P**(2/3) or P**(3/4) reflecting surface-to-volume ratios
- Gompertz-type deceleration → Logarithmic dependence on population: P*log(P) structure indicating multiplicative decline in per-capita rate
- Immigration or constant influx → Additive constant term independent of P in the growth rate expression
- Seasonal or periodic forcing → Trigonometric modulation sin(c0*t) or cos(c0*t) multiplying growth terms
- Carrying capacity saturation → Per-capita growth rate (dP_dt/P) is a decreasing function of P, often linear or concave
- Time-lagged effects approximated → Polynomial or exponential functions of t appearing as multiplicative modifiers to P-dependent terms
